Looking at CuTe source code / paper for composition:\n\nThe key idea: given A and B, where A has shapes/strides and B has shapes/strides, we need to find R such that R(i) = A(B(i)).\n\nFor rank-1 A and rank-1 B:\n- If B has stride 0: R = (Sb, 0) - just replicate the first element\n- Otherwise: R = (Sb, Da * Db) but we need to be careful\n\nWait, the more general case. Let me think again.\n\nActually, for CuTe composition, the general idea is:\n\nIf A = a0:a1:a2 (three modes in coalesced form, meaning each mode maps its coordinate space to an index) and B = b0:b1 (two modes), then:\n\nThe composition AâB replaces some modes of A. Specifically, B's \"active\" coordinates become new modes in the result.\n\nLet me look at this from the CuTe perspective more carefully.\n\nActually, I think the key algorithm is:\n\nFor `composition(A, B)` where A and B are Layouts:\n\n1. Using \"coalesced modes\":\n- The outer mode has shape 6, stride 15\n- The inner mode has shape 15, stride 1\n- B[0] has stride 5\n- The inner stride 1 * 5 = 5\n- But shape-wise, B replacing the inner mode: we'd need B's shape to relate to inner shape\n\nHmm, I think the approach might be about replacing individual modes of A:\n\nIf we replace the inner mode of A (shape 15, stride 1) with B[0] (shape 2, stride 5):\nResult = (6, 2):(15, 5)\n\nCheck: R(k) = crd2idx(k, (6,2), (15,5))\nR(0) = crd2idx(0, (6,2), (15,5)) = 0*15 + 0*5 = 0\nR(1) = crd2idx(1, (6,2), (15,5)) = 1%2=1, 1//2=0 â 1*15 + 0*5 = 15\nR(2) = crd2idx(2, (6,2), (15,5)) = 2%2=0, 2//2=1 â 0*15 + 1*5 = 5\n\nSo R(0)=0, R(1)=15, R(2)=5.\n\nBut A(B(0))=0, A(B(1))=75, A(B(2))=...B(2)=10, A(10):\ncrd2idx(10, (6,15), (15,1)) = 10%6=4, 10//6=1 â 4*15 + 1*1 = 61\n\nR(2) should be 61, not 5. So the mode-replacement approach doesn't work directly.\n\nI think I'm overcomplicating this. Let me go back to basics.\n\nThe fundamental definition: R(c) = A(B(c)) for all c in R's domain.\n\nFor the general case, the algorithm should compute the correct result. Let me think about what approach produces the correct mapping.\n\nActually, let me reconsider the task description again:\n\n\"stride-zero `layoutB`: return a stride-zero layout with `layoutB.shape`.\"\n\"general rank-1 `layoutB`: use coalesced modes of `layoutA` to compute the composed shape and stride.\"\n\nI think \"use coalesced modes\" means: the composition replaces the coalesced modes of A. If A coalesces to rank-1, the result is simple. If A doesn't fully coalesce, then...\n\nActually, maybe the test cases are designed so that one of these scenarios always holds:\n1. B is None\n2. B is int\n3. B is a tuple\n4. B.shape is a tuple\n5. B has zero stride\n6. A fully coalesces to rank-1\n\nIn scenario 6, the result would be straightforward.\n\nOR, maybe scenario 6 means: A may not fully coalesce, but the algorithm handles it correctly by composing with just the last coalesced mode or something.\n\nLet me try yet another approach. Let me look at what result makes sense.\n\nIf A coalesces to (a0, a1):(d0, d1) (rank-2) and B = (Sb, Db):\n\nThe composed result R should be:\n- The outer part of A (a0, d0) stays the same\n- The inner part (a1, d1) is replaced by B\n\nSo R = (a0, Sb):(d0, d1 * Db)?\n\nBut what if Sb > a1? Then B maps outside the inner mode's range.\n\nHmm, in that case, B \"wraps around\" to the outer mode. But in the composition semantics, B maps linearly, so it doesn't wrapâit just maps to larger coordinates.\n\nWait, I think the correct interpretation is:\n\nB maps into the cosize-space of A (the linear index space), not into A's coordinate space.\n\nNo wait, let me re-read: B maps logical coordinates to linear indices, and A maps logical coordinates to linear indices. R = A â B means: first apply B to get a linear index, then apply A to that linear index.\n\nSo B maps to a linear coordinate in [0, cosize(B)-1], and this linear coordinate is used as input to A.\n\nActually, looking at this again: A expects logical coordinates (not linear indices). When we call A(x) where x is a single integer, A treats x as a \"flattened\" logical coordinate and uses crd2idx to compute the linear index.\n\nSo A(B(k)) really means: compute the linear index B(k), then treat that as a flattened coordinate into A's logical space, and compute crd2idx(B(k), A.shape, A.stride).\n\nOK so now let me think about the coalescing approach:\n\nIf we coalesce A to get A_c, then A_c(k) = A(k) for all k in [0, size(A)-1] (coalescing preserves the function, just changes the representation).\n\nIf A_c is rank-1 (Sa, Da), then A_c(k) = k * Da.\nSo R(k) = A(B(k)) = A_c(B(k)) = B(k) * Da = k * Db * Da.\nR = (Sb, Da * Db). Done!\n\nIf A_c is rank-2 ((a0, a1), (d0, d1)):\nA_c(k) = crd2idx(k, (a0, a1), (d0, d1))\nR(k) = A_c(B(k)) = A_c(k * Db)\n\nFor k * Db < a0: R(k) = k * Db * d0\nFor a0 <= k * Db < 2*a0: R(k) = (k*Db - a0) * d0 + d1\n\nThis is only linear if d0 * a0 == d1, which we said it's not (that's why we couldn't coalesce).\n\nSo the result is genuinely nonlinear, and therefore cannot be represented as a single rank-1 layout.\n\nHmm, but the CuTe library always returns a Layout from composition. So maybe:\n\nR = Layout((a0_composed, a1_composed), (d0_composed, d1_composed))\n\nWhere:\n- a0_composed relates to how B interacts with the first mode of A_c\n- a1_composed relates to how B interacts with the second mode of A_c\n\nLet me think...\n\nB has shape Sb and stride Db. B maps k â k * Db for k in [0, Sb-1].\n\nIn A_c, coordinates are (i, j) where i â [0, a0-1], j â [0, a1-1], and the linear coordinate is i + a0 * j.\n\nFor B's output to be a valid coordinate in A_c's space, we need B(k) < size(A_c) = a0 * a1.\n\nNow, B(k) = k * Db. As k ranges over [0, Sb-1], B(k) takes values 0, Db, 2*Db, ..., (Sb-1)*Db.\n\nThe number of B-values that fall in the \"first row\" (i.e., linear coords 0 to a0-1) is min(Sb, ceil(a0/Db)).\n\nActually, let's be more precise. B(k) = k*Db. The first row of A_c is coordinates [0, a0). We need k*Db < a0, so k < a0/Db. The number of such k values is min(Sb, ceil(a0/Db) or floor, depending on exact boundary).\n\nHmm, this is getting messy. Let me try to think about it differently.\n\nMaybe the composition result for rank-1 B with multi-mode A_c is:\n\nR = make_layout(mode_compose(A_c[i], B) for each mode i)\n\nwhere mode_compose means something like: for the first mode, compose normally, and for subsequent modes, adjust based on how B \"spills over\" from the previous modes.\n\nActually, I think this might be the right track. Let me think about it as follows:\n\nFor A_c = (a0, a1):(d0, d1) and B = (Sb, Db):\n\n1. The \"scratch space\" for mode 1 of A_c is a0 elements.\n2. B has Sb elements, each stepping by Db.\n3. The i = 0 position of B maps to linear coord 0 in A_c.\n4. The number of B elements that fit within one \"row\" of A_c's first mode:\n   m0 = divup(a0, Db) if Db > 0 else ... hmm, what about Db = 0?\n   Actually, if Db = 0, all B coords map to 0, which is handled by the stride-zero case.\n\nLet me just consider Db > 0 for now.\n\nNumber of B elements that stay within a0/Db: \nThe elements k where k*Db < a0: k < a0/Db.\nSo count = min(Sb, floor((a0 - 1) / Db) + 1) = min(Sb, ceil(a0 / Db))\n\nHmm, this doesn't simplify nicely into a layout operation.\n\nOK I think I need to look at the actual CuTe composition algorithm. Try to compose A's rightmost mode with B\n2. If that fails (B's shape exceeds A's rightmost mode), combine more modes\n\nActually, I think the correct CuTe algorithm for rank-1 composition is:\n\nGiven A (possibly multi-mode) and B (rank-1):\n\n1. Coalesce A to get A_c\n2. If A_c is rank-1:\n   R = Layout(Sb, stride(A_c) * stride(B))\n3. If A_c is multi-mode:\n   R = compose_inner(A_c, B)\n   \nWhere compose_inner handles the general case by:\n- B replaces the \"inner\" structure of A_c\n- For each mode of A_c (from innermost outward), determine the new shape/stride\n\nActually, let me try yet another approach. Let me check what the CuTe library does by looking at the CUTLASS source.\n\nActually, let me try this: let me fetch the paper mentioned in the task.\n\nActually, the task says \"The reference source for the math is Cris Cecka, 'CuTe Layout Representation and Algebra', arXiv:2603.02298.\"\n\nLet me look at the paper.","time":{"start":1784660795395,"end":1784660990955}}}

These instructions prescribe fixed, often complex data layouts that must be correctly propagated through the entire execution pipeline to ensure both correctness and optimal performance. We present CuTe, a novel mathematical specification for representing and manipulating tensors. CuTe introduces two key innovations: (1) a hierarchical layout representation that directly extends traditional flat-shape and flat-stride tensor representations, enabling the representation of complex mappings required by modern hardware instructions, and (2) a rich algebra of layout operations -- including concatenation, coalescence, composition, complementation, division, tiling, and inversion -- that enables sophisticated layout manipulation, derivation, verification, and static analysis. CuTe layouts provide a framework for managing both data layouts and thread arrangements in GPU kernels, while the layout algebra enables powerful compile-time reasoning about layout properties and the expression of generic tensor transformations.  \n> In this work, we demonstrate that CuTe's abstractions significantly aid software development compared to traditional approaches, promote compile-time verification of architecturally prescribed layouts, facilitate the implementation of algorithmic primitives that generalize to a wide range of applications, and enable the concise expression of tiling and partitioning patterns required by modern specialized tensor instructions.  \n> CuTe has been successfully deployed in production systems, forming the foundation of NVIDIA's CUTLASS library and a number of related efforts including CuTe DSL.\n\nSubjects:\n\nMathematical Software (cs.MS); Programming Languages (cs.PL)\n\nCite as:\n\n[arXiv:2603.02298](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.02298) is_integral<Shape >::value);\n  static_assert(is_tuple<Stride>::value || is_integral<Stride>::value);\n  return Layout<Shape,Stride>(shape, stride);\n}\n\ntemplate <class Shape>\nCUTE_HOST_DEVICE compact_major<LayoutLeft>(shape));\n}\n\n//\n// Convenience tags for common layouts\n//\n\ntemplate <class Shape>\nCUTE_HOST_DEVICE constexpr\nauto\nmake_layout(Shape const& shape, LayoutLeft)\n{\n  return make_layout(shape, compact_major<LayoutLeft>(shape));\n}\n\ntemplate <class Shape>\nCUTE_HOST_DEVICE constexpr\nauto\nmake_layout(Shape const& shape, LayoutRight)\n{\n  return make_layout(shape, compact_major<LayoutRight>(shape));\n}\n\n//\n// Construct a layout from multiple layouts by concatenation\n//\n\n// One argument overload\ntemplate <class Shape0, class Stride0>\nCUTE_HOST_DEVICE constexpr\nauto\nmake_layout(Layout<Shape0,Stride0> const& layout0)\n{\n  return make_layout(make_shape (layout0.shape() ),\n                     make_stride(layout0.stride()));\n}\n\n// Two argument overload\ntemplate <class Shape0, class Stride0,\n          class Shape1, class Stride1>\nCUTE_HOST_DEVICE constexpr\nauto\nmake_layout(Layout<Shape0,Stride0> const& layout0,\n            Layout<Shape1,Stride1> const& layout1)\n{\n  return make_layout(make_shape (layout0.shape() , layout1.shape() ),\n                     make_stride(layout0.stride(), layout1.stride()));\n}\n\n// Var argument overload\ntemplate <class Shape0, class Stride0,\n          class Shape1, class Stride1,\n          class... Shapes, class... Strides>\nCUTE_HOST_DEVICE constexpr\nauto\nmake_layout(Layout<Shape0,Stride0> const& layout0,\n            Layout<Shape1,Stride1> const& layout1,\n            Layout<Shapes,Strides> const&... layouts)\n{\n  return make_layout(make_shape (layout0.shape() , layout1.shape() , layouts.shape()... ),\n                     make_stride(layout0.stride(), layout1.stride(), layouts.stride()...));\n}\n\n//\n// Advanced Layout constructions\n//\n\n// Make a compact layout with shape @a shape and strides following the order induced by @a order.\n// Dynamic values in @a order are ignored, considered large, and considered ordered from left to right.\n// Example:\n//   make_ordered_layout(Shape<_2,_2,_2,_2>{}, Step<_0,_2,_3,_1>{})\n//     ->  (_2,_2,_2,_2):(_1,_4,_8,_2)\n//   make_ordered_layout(make_shape(2,3,4,5), make_step(Int<2>{}, 67, 42, Int<50>{}))\n//     -> (2,3,4,5):(_1,10,30,2)\ntemplate <class Shape, class Order>\nCUTE_HOST_DEVICE constexpr\nauto\nmake_ordered_layout(Shape const& shape, Order const& order)\n{\n  return make_layout(shape, compact_order(shape, order));\n}\n\n// Make a compact layout with the same shape as @a layout\n//   and strides following the order induced by @a layout.stride().\n// Static-0 strides in the input @a layout are preserved in the output.\n// Example:\n//   make_layout_like(Layout<Shape<_2,_2,_2,_2>, Stride<_0,_2,_4,_1>>{})\n//     ->  (_2,_2,_2,_2):(_0,_2,_4,_1)\n//   make_layout_like(make_layout(make_shape(2,3,4,5), make_stride(Int<0>{},42,Int<1>{},Int<0>{})))\n//     -> (2,3,4,5):(_0,4,_1,_0)\ntemplate <class Shape, class Stride>\nCUTE_HOST_DEVICE constexpr\nauto\nmake_layout_like(Layout<Shape,Stride> const& layout)\n{\n  return make_layout(layout.shape(),\n                     compact_order(filter_zeros(layout.stride(), layout.shape()), layout.stride()));\n}\n\n// Make a compact layout with the same shape as @a layout\n//   and strides following the order induced by @a layout.stride(),\n//   except mode-0 is always stride-1 and generated column-major.\n// The 0th mode is commonly used for MMA_Atoms or Copy_Atoms so this\n//   generates the 0th mode with LayoutLeft (preserving stride-0s) regardless of the reference layout\ntemplate <class Shape, class Stride>\nCUTE_HOST_DEVICE constexpr\nauto\nmake_fragment_like(Layout<Shape,Stride> const& layout)\n{\n  constexpr int R = Layout<Shape,Stride>::rank;\n  if constexpr (R > 1 && is_static<Shape>::value) {\n    return tiled_product(make_layout(get<0>(layout.shape()),\n                                     compact_major<LayoutLeft>(filter_zeros(get<0>(layout.stride()), get<0>(layout.shape())))),\n                         make_ordered_layout(take<1,R>(layout.shape()), take<1,R>(layout.stride())));\n  } else {\n    return make_layout(layout.shape());\n  }\n\n  CUTE_GCC_UNREACHABLE;\n}\n\ntemplate <class Shape,\n          __CUTE_REQUIRES(is_tuple<Shape>::value || is_integral<Shape>::value)>\nCUTE_HOST_DEVICE constexpr\nauto\nmake_fragment_like(Shape const& shape)\n{\n  return make_layout(shape);\n}\n\n//\n// Make an identity layout that maps a coordinate to itself\n//\n\ntemplate <class Shape>\nCUTE_HOST_DEVICE constexpr\nauto\nmake_identity_layout(Shape const& shape)\n{\n  return make_layout(shape, make_basis_like(shape));\n}\n\n//\n// Operations to manipulate Layouts like a tuple of pairs\n//\n\n// Return the Is...th sublayout.\n// For Is... = <I0,I1,...,IN>, equivalent to get<IN>(...get<I1>(get<I0>(layout)))\ntemplate <size_t... Is, class Shape, class Stride>\nCUTE_HOST_DEVICE constexpr\nauto\nget(Layout<Shape,Stride> const& layout)\n{\n  return make_layout(get<Is...>(layout.shape()),\n                     get<Is...>(layout.stride()));\n}\n\n// Return a new layout with only the modes in the range [B,E)\ntemplate <int B, int E, class Shape, class Stride>\nCUTE_HOST_DEVICE constexpr\nauto\ntake(Layout<Shape,Stride> const& layout)\n{\n  static_assert(B < E, \"take: empty range error\");\n  static_assert(0 <= B && E <= Layout<Shape,Stride>::rank, \"take: range out of bounds\");\n  return make_layout(take<B,E>(layout.shape()),\n                     take<B,E>(layout.stride()));\n}\n\n// Return a new layout with only the modes Is... = <I0,I1,...,IN>\ntemplate <int... Is, class Shape, class Stride>\nCUTE_HOST_DEVICE constexpr\nauto\nselect(Layout<Shape,Stride> const& layout)\n{\n  return make_layout(select<Is...>(layout.shape()),\n                     select<Is...>(layout.stride()));\n}\n\n// Return a layout with depth at most 1\ntemplate <class Shape, class Stride>\nCUTE_HOST_DEVICE constexpr\nauto\nflatten(Layout<Shape,Stride> const& layout)\n{\n  return make_layout(flatten(layout.shape()),\n                     flatten(layout.stride()));\n}\n\n// Return a layout whose profile is congruent to TargetProfile\n// @pre Input layout is flat, flatten(@a layout) == @a layout\n// @pre Input layout can be folded to profile, rank(@a layout) == rank(flatten(@a target_profile))\n// @post congruent(@a result, @a target_profile)\ntemplate <class Shape, class Stride, class TargetProfile>\nCUTE_HOST_DEVICE constexpr\nauto\nunflatten(Layout<Shape,Stride> const& layout, TargetProfile const& target_profile)\n{\n  return make_layout(unflatten(layout.shape(),  target_profile),\n                     unflatten(layout.stride(), target_profile));\n}\n\n//\n// Utilities\n//\n\n// Return the sublayout of mode I...\ntemplate <int... Is, class Shape, class Stride>\nCUTE_HOST_DEVICE constexpr\ndecltype(auto)\nlayout(Layout<Shape,Stride> const& layout)\n{\n  if constexpr (sizeof...(Is) == 0) {\n    return layout;\n  } else {\n    return get<Is...>(layout);\n  }\n\n  CUTE_GCC_UNREACHABLE;\n}\n\n// Return the shape of a mode\ntemplate <int... Is, class Shape, class Stride>\nCUTE_HOST_DEVICE constexpr\ndecltype(auto)\nshape(Layout<Shape,Stride>& layout)\n{\n  return layout.template shape<Is...>();\n}\n\ntemplate <int... Is, class Shape, class Stride>\nCUTE_HOST_DEVICE constexpr\ndecltype(auto)\nshape(Layout<Shape,Stride> const& layout)\n{\n  return layout.template shape<Is...>();\n}\n\n// Return the stride of a mode\ntemplate <int... Is, class Shape, class Stride>\nCUTE_HOST_DEVICE constexpr\ndecltype(auto)\nstride(Layout<Shape,Stride>& layout)\n{\n  return layout.template stride<Is...>();\n}\n\ntemplate <int... Is, class Shape, class Stride>\nCUTE_HOST_DEVICE constexpr\ndecltype(auto)\nstride(Layout<Shape,Stride> const& layout)\n{\n  return layout.template stride<Is...>();\n}\n\n// Return the number of elements in a mode\ntemplate <int... Is, class Shape, class Stride>\nCUTE_HOST_DEVICE constexpr\nauto\nsize(Layout<Shape,Stride> const& layout)\n{\n  return size(shape<Is...>(layout));\n}\n\n// Return the number of modes\ntemplate <int... Is, class Shape, class Stride>\nCUTE_HOST_DEVICE constexpr\nauto\nrank(Layout<Shape,Stride> const& layout)\n{\n  return rank(shape<Is...>(layout));\n}\n\n// Return the depth of the layout\ntemplate <int... Is, class Shape, class Stride>\nCUTE_HOST_DEVICE constexpr\nauto\ndepth(Layout<Shape,Stride> const& layout)\n{\n  return depth(shape<Is...>(layout));\n}\n\n// Return the coprofile of a mode as a tuple of _0s\n// @post congruent(coprofile(@a layout), @a layout(i)) for any i\n// @return T Tuple that is congruent with the codomain of @a a.\ntemplate <int... Is, class Shape, class Stride>\nCUTE_HOST_DEVICE constexpr\nauto\ncoprofile(Layout<Shape,Stride> const& layout)\n{\n  return repeat_like(as_arithmetic_tuple(sum(stride<Is...>(layout))), Int<0>{});\n}\n\n// Return the codomain shape of a mode\n// @post size(coshape(@a layout)) == cosize(@a layout)\n// @return C Coordinate with smallest elements such that\n//           elem_less(@a sub_layout(c), C) for all c < size(@a sub_layout)\n//           where @a sub_layout = get<Is...>(layout).\ntemplate <int... Is, class Shape, class Stride>\nCUTE_HOST_DEVICE constexpr\nauto\ncoshape(Layout<Shape,Stride> const& layout)\n{\n  auto m1_shapes   = transform_leaf( shape<Is...>(layout), [](auto s) { return s - Int<1>{}; });\n  auto abs_strides = transform_leaf(stride<Is...>(layout), abs_fn{});\n  auto co_coord    = as_arithmetic_tuple(inner_product(m1_shapes, abs_strides));\n  return transform_leaf(co_coord, [](auto c) { return c + Int<1>{}; });\n}\n\n// Return the codomain size of a mode\n// @return M smallest integer such that\n//           size(@a sub_layout(c)) < M for all c < size(@a sub_layout)\n//           where @a sub_layout = get<Is...>(layout).\ntemplate <int... Is, class Shape, class Stride>\nCUTE_HOST_DEVICE constexpr\nauto\ncosize(Layout<Shape,Stride> const& layout)\n{\n  return size(coshape<Is...>(layout));\n}\n\ntemplate <class Layout>\nusing cosize_t = decltype(cosize(declval<Layout>()));\n\ntemplate <class Layout>\nstatic constexpr auto cosize_v = cosize_t<Layout>::value;\n\n// With crd2idx(coord, shape), makes sense to have crd2idx(coord, Layout) as well\ntemplate <class Coord, class Shape, class Stride>\nCUTE_HOST_DEVICE constexpr\nauto\ncrd2idx(Coord const& c, Layout<Shape,Stride> const& layout)\n{\n  return crd2idx(c, layout.shape(), layout.stride());\n}\n\n//\n// Slice and Dice a layout\n//\n\ntemplate <class Coord, class Shape, class Stride>\nCUTE_HOST_DEVICE constexpr\nauto\nslice(Coord const& c, Layout<Shape,Stride> const& layout)\n{\n  return make_layout(slice(c, layout.shape()),\n                     slice(c, layout.stride()));\n}\n\ntemplate <class Coord, class Shape, class Stride>\nCUTE_HOST_DEVICE constexpr\nauto\nslice_and_offset(Coord const& c, Layout<Shape,Stride> const& layout)\n{\n  return cute::make_tuple(slice(c, layout), crd2idx(c, layout));\n}\n\ntemplate <class Coord, class Shape, class Stride>\nCUTE_HOST_DEVICE constexpr\nauto\ndice(Coord const& c, Layout<Shape,Stride> const& layout)\n{\n  return make_layout(dice(c, layout.shape()),\n                     dice(c, layout.stride()));\n}\n\n// Compute a pointer offset and (potentially modified) layout from a coordinate\n// This exists so it can be overloaded for ComposedLayout\ntemplate <class Coord, class Shape, class Stride>\nCUTE_HOST_DEVICE constexpr\nauto\ndomain_offset(Coord const& coord, Layout<Shape,Stride> const& layout)\n{\n  return cute::make_tuple(layout, layout(coord));\n}\n\n//\n// Transform the modes of a layout\n//\n\nnamespace detail {\n\ntemplate <class Tuple, class F, int... I>\nCUTE_HOST_DEVICE constexpr\nauto\ntransform_layout(Tuple const& t, F&& f, seq<I...>)\n{\n  return make_layout(f(get<I>(t))...);\n}\n\ntemplate <class Tuple0, class Tuple1, class F, int... I, int... I0, int... I1>\nCUTE_HOST_DEVICE constexpr\nauto\ntransform_layout(Tuple0 const& t0, Tuple1 const& t1, F&& f, seq<I...>, seq<I0...>, seq<I1...>)\n{\n  return make_layout(f(get<I>(t0),get<I>(t1))..., get<I0>(t0)..., get<I1>(t1)...);\n}\n\n} // end namespace detail\n\ntemplate <class Tuple, class F>\nCUTE_HOST_DEVICE constexpr\nauto\ntransform_layout(Tuple const& t, F&& f)\n{\n  return detail::transform_layout(t, f, make_seq<decltype(rank(t))::value>{});\n}\n\ntemplate <class Tuple0, class Tuple1, class F>\nCUTE_HOST_DEVICE constexpr\nauto\ntransform_layout(Tuple0 const& t0, Tuple1 const& t1, F&& f)\n{\n  constexpr int R0 = decltype(rank(t0))::value;\n  constexpr int R1 = decltype(rank(t1))::value;\n  constexpr int R  = (R0 < R1) ? R0 : R1;\n  return detail::transform_layout(t0, t1, f, make_seq<R>{}, make_range<R,R0>{}, make_range<R,R1>{});\n}\n\n//\n// Coalesce and Filter\n//\n\nnamespace detail {\n\n// Look at each element and the front of the stack (in order of priority)\n// front(NewLayout)  get<I>(Layout)\n//      s0:d0           _1:d1     =>  continue\n//      _1:d0           s1:d1     =>  replace_front    s1:d1\n//      s0:s1*d1        s1:d1     =>  replace_front s0*s1:d1\n//      s0:d0           s1:d1     =>  prepend          s1:d1\n//\n// @pre OldShape and OldStride are flat\ntemplate <int I, class OldShape, class OldStride, class NewShape, class NewStride>\nCUTE_HOST_DEVICE constexpr\nauto\nbw_coalesce(OldShape const& old_shape, OldStride const& old_stride,\n            NewShape const& new_shape, NewStride const& new_stride)\n{\n  if constexpr (I == -1) {\n    // Base case, we're done\n    if constexpr (is_constant<1, NewShape>::value) {\n      return Layout<_1,_0>{};\n    } else {\n      return Layout<NewShape,NewStride>{new_shape,new_stride};\n    }\n  } else if constexpr (is_constant<1, decltype(get<I>(old_shape))>::value) {\n    // shape<I>(layout) == _1, skip it and continue\n    return bw_coalesce<I-1>(old_shape, old_stride, new_shape, new_stride);\n  } else if constexpr (is_constant<1, NewShape>::value) {\n    // Replace our shape-1 with anything (Can only happen on input new_shape/new_stride)\n    return bw_coalesce<I-1>(old_shape, old_stride, get<I>(old_shape), get<I>(old_stride));\n  } else if constexpr (is_static<decltype(get<0>(new_shape))>::value &&\n                       is_constant<true, decltype(get<I>(old_shape) * get<I>(old_stride) == get<0>(new_stride))>::value) {\n    // Merge modes because the shapes and strides match\n    return bw_coalesce<I-1>(old_shape, old_stride,\n                            replace_front(new_shape,  get<I>(old_shape) * get<0>(new_shape)),\n                            replace_front(new_stride, get<I>(old_stride)));\n  } else {\n    // Can't replace or merge, so prepend a new mode\n    return bw_coalesce<I-1>(old_shape, old_stride,\n                            prepend(new_shape,  get<I>(old_shape)),\n                            prepend(new_stride, get<I>(old_stride)));\n  }\n\n  CUTE_GCC_UNREACHABLE;\n}\n\n// cute::coalesce promises to not change the Layout as a function from integers to codomain.\n// It accomplishes this inside of the Layout's domain, but not always outside of the domain.\n//   Example: (_4,_1):(_1,_0) coalesces to _4:_1.\n// detail::coalesce_x preserves the Layout function inside its domain and outside.\n//\n// @post depth(@a result) <= 1\n// @post for all i, 0 <= i, @a layout(i) == @a result(i)\ntemplate <class Shape, class Stride>\nCUTE_HOST_DEVICE constexpr\nauto\ncoalesce_x(Layout<Shape,Stride> const& layout)\n{\n  auto flat_shape  = flatten(layout.shape());\n  auto flat_stride = flatten(layout.stride());\n\n  constexpr int R = decltype(rank(flat_shape))::value;\n  if constexpr (is_constant<1, decltype(get<R-1>(flat_shape))>::value) {\n    return detail::bw_coalesce<R-2>(flat_shape, flat_stride,             Int<2>{}, get<R-1>(flat_stride));\n  } else {\n    return detail::bw_coalesce<R-2>(flat_shape, flat_stride, get<R-1>(flat_shape), get<R-1>(flat_stride));\n  }\n\n  CUTE_GCC_UNREACHABLE;\n}\n\n// Apply coalesce_x at the terminals of trg_profile\ntemplate <class Shape, class Stride, class IntTuple>\nCUTE_HOST_DEVICE constexpr\nauto\ncoalesce_x(Layout<Shape,Stride> const& layout, IntTuple const& trg_profile)\n{\n  if constexpr (is_tuple<IntTuple>::value) {\n    static_assert(tuple_size<IntTuple>::value <= Layout<Shape,Stride>::rank);\n    return cute::transform_layout(layout, trg_profile, [](auto const& l, auto const& t) { return coalesce_x(l,t); });\n  } else {\n    return coalesce_x(layout);\n  }\n\n  CUTE_GCC_UNREACHABLE;\n}\n\n} // end namespace detail\n\n// \"Simplify\" the layout by combining modes that are possible to combine\n// Does not respect the shape of the layout, but does preserve total size\n// @post size(@a result) == size(@a layout)\n// @post depth(@a result) <= 1\n// @post for all i, 0 <= i < size(@a layout), @a layout(i) == @a result(i)\ntemplate <class Shape, class Stride>\nCUTE_HOST_DEVICE constexpr\nauto\ncoalesce(Layout<Shape,Stride> const& layout)\n{\n  auto flat_shape  = flatten(layout.shape());\n  auto flat_stride = flatten(layout.stride());\n\n  constexpr int R = decltype(rank(flat_shape))::value;\n  return detail::bw_coalesce<R-2>(flat_shape, flat_stride, get<R-1>(flat_shape), get<R-1>(flat_stride));\n}\n\n// Apply coalesce at the terminals of trg_profile\ntemplate <class Shape, class Stride, class IntTuple>\nCUTE_HOST_DEVICE constexpr\nauto\ncoalesce(Layout<Shape,Stride> const& layout, IntTuple const& trg_profile)\n{\n  if constexpr (is_tuple<IntTuple>::value) {\n    static_assert(tuple_size<IntTuple>::value <= Layout<Shape,Stride>::rank);\n    return transform_layout(layout, trg_profile, [](auto const& l, auto const& t) { return coalesce(l,t); });\n  } else {\n    return coalesce(layout);\n  }\n\n  CUTE_GCC_UNREACHABLE;\n}\n\n// Combine static and dynamic modes of a shape.\n// @post size(@a result) == size(@a shape)\n// @post depth(@a result) <= 1\ntemplate <class Shape>\nCUTE_HOST_DEVICE constexpr\nauto\ncoalesce(Shape const& shape)\n{\n  static_assert(is_integral<Shape>::value || is_tuple<Shape>::value);\n\n  return cute::fold_first(flatten(shape), [](auto const& init, auto const& a) {\n    if constexpr (is_static<decltype(back(init))>::value == is_static<decltype(a)>::value) {\n      return replace_back(init, back(init) * a);  // Both static or both dynamic, coalesce and replace\n    } else {\n      return append(init, a);                     // Can't coalesce, so append\n    }\n\n    CUTE_GCC_UNREACHABLE;\n  });\n}\n\n// Replace the modes in layout that have a 0-stride with a 1-size\ntemplate <class Shape, class Stride>\nCUTE_HOST_DEVICE constexpr\nauto\nfilter_zeros(Layout<Shape,Stride> const& layout)\n{\n  return make_layout(filter_zeros(layout.stride(), layout.shape()), layout.stride());\n}\n\n// Replace the modes in layout that correspond to a 0 at the terminals of trg_profile with a 1-size\ntemplate <class Shape, class Stride, class IntTuple>\nCUTE_HOST_DEVICE constexpr\nauto\nfilter_zeros(Layout<Shape,Stride> const& layout, IntTuple const& trg_profile)\n{\n  return make_layout(filter_zeros(trg_profile, layout.shape()), layout.stride());\n}\n\n// Remove all of the 0-strides and 1-sizes\n// Return 1-shape if empty\ntemplate <class Shape, class Stride>\nCUTE_HOST_DEVICE constexpr\nauto\nfilter(Layout<Shape,Stride> const& layout)\n{\n  return coalesce(filter_zeros(layout));\n}\n\n// Apply filter at the terminals of trg_profile\ntemplate <class Shape, class Stride, class IntTuple>\nCUTE_HOST_DEVICE constexpr\nauto\nfilter(Layout<Shape,Stride> const& layout, IntTuple const& trg_profile)\n{\n  if constexpr (is_tuple<IntTuple>::value) {\n    static_assert(tuple_size<IntTuple>::value <= Layout<Shape,Stride>::rank);\n    return transform_layout(layout, trg_profile, [](auto const& l, auto const& t) { return filter(l,t); });\n  } else {\n    return filter(layout);\n  }\n\n  CUTE_GCC_UNREACHABLE;\n}\n\n//\n// Append, Prepend, Replace\n//\n\ntemplate <int N, class ShapeA, class StrideA, class ShapeX = _1, class StrideX = _0>\nCUTE_HOST_DEVICE constexpr\nauto\nappend(Layout<ShapeA,StrideA> const& layout,\n       Layout<ShapeX,StrideX> const& x = {})\n{\n  return make_layout(append<N>(layout.shape(),  x.shape()),\n                     append<N>(layout.stride(), x.stride()));\n}\n\ntemplate <class ShapeA, class StrideA, class ShapeX = _1, class StrideX = _0>\nCUTE_HOST_DEVICE constexpr\nauto\nappend(Layout<ShapeA,StrideA> const& layout,\n       Layout<ShapeX,StrideX> const& x = {})\n{\n  return make_layout(append(layout.shape(),  x.shape()),\n                     append(layout.stride(), x.stride()));\n}\n\ntemplate <int N, class ShapeA, class StrideA, class ShapeX = _1, class StrideX = _0>\nCUTE_HOST_DEVICE constexpr\nauto\nprepend(Layout<ShapeA,StrideA> const& layout,\n        Layout<ShapeX,StrideX> const& x = {})\n{\n  return make_layout(prepend<N>(layout.shape(),  x.shape()),\n                     prepend<N>(layout.stride(), x.stride()));\n}\n\ntemplate <class ShapeA, class StrideA, class ShapeX = _1, class StrideX = _0>\nCUTE_HOST_DEVICE constexpr\nauto\nprepend(Layout<ShapeA,StrideA> const& layout,\n        Layout<ShapeX,StrideX> const& x = {})\n{\n  return make_layout(prepend(layout.shape(),  x.shape()),\n                     prepend(layout.stride(), x.stride()));\n}\n\ntemplate <int N, class ShapeA, class StrideA, class ShapeX, class StrideX>\nCUTE_HOST_DEVICE constexpr\nauto\nreplace(Layout<ShapeA,StrideA> const& layout,\n        Layout<ShapeX,StrideX> const& x)\n{\n  return make_layout(replace<N>(layout.shape(),  x.shape()),\n                     replace<N>(layout.stride(), x.stride()));\n}\n\ntemplate <int B, int E, class Shape, class Stride>\nCUTE_HOST_DEVICE constexpr\nauto\ngroup(Layout<Shape,Stride> const& layout)\n{\n  return make_layout(group<B,E>(layout.shape()),\n                     group<B,E>(layout.stride()));\n}\n\n//\n// Composition of two layouts: lhs o rhs\n// @post compatible(rhs, result)\n// @post result(c) = lhs(rhs(c))\n//         for all c in the domain of rhs\n//\n\nnamespace detail {\n\ntemplate <class LShape, class LStride,\n          class RShape, class RStride>\nCUTE_HOST_DEVICE constexpr\nauto\ncomposition_impl(LShape const& lhs_shape, [[maybe_unused]] LStride const& lhs_stride,\n                 RShape const& rhs_shape, RStride const& rhs_stride)\n{\n  if constexpr (is_tuple<RShape>::value) {                 // Right-distributivity of Layout composition for RHS tuple\n    return transform_layout(rhs_shape, rhs_stride, [&](auto const& s, auto const& d) {\n      return composition_impl(lhs_shape, lhs_stride, s, d);\n    });\n  } else\n  if constexpr (is_scaled_basis<RStride>::value) {         // Special case for a RHS ScaledBasis stride\n    return composition_impl(basis_get(rhs_stride, lhs_shape), basis_get(rhs_stride, lhs_stride),\n                            rhs_shape, basis_value(rhs_stride));\n  } else\n  if constexpr (is_constant<0, RStride>::value) {          // Special case shortcut for any RHS static stride-0\n    return Layout<RShape, RStride>{rhs_shape, rhs_stride};\n  } else\n  if constexpr (is_integral<LShape>::value) {              // Special case shortcut for any LHS integral shape\n    return Layout{rhs_shape, rhs_stride * lhs_stride};\n  } else {                                                 // General case: LHS tuple, RHS integral\n    constexpr int R = tuple_size<LShape>::value;\n\n    auto [result_shape, result_stride, rest_shape, rest_stride] =\n      cute::fold(make_seq<R-1>{},                           // t = [0,1,2,...,R-1)\n                 cute::make_tuple(cute::tuple<>{},          // v = (result_shape,\n                                  cute::tuple<>{},          //      result_stride,\n Coalesce LHS to get a flat layout (using coprofile of RHS for guidance)\n2. Then apply composition_impl\n\nThe `coalesce_x` with coprofile is important. Let me understand coprofile:\n```cpp\ntemplate <int... Is, class Shape, class Stride>\nCUTE_HOST_DEVICE constexpr\nauto\ncoprofile(Layout<Shape,Stride> const& layout)\n{\n  return repeat_like(as_arithmetic_tuple(sum(stride<Is...>(layout))), Int<0>{});\n}\n```\n\nThe coprofile is a tuple of zeros that has the same structure as the stride. Since our RHS is rank-1, the coprofile is just a single 0 value.\n\nSo `coalesce_x(lhs, 0)` which is just `coalesce_x(lhs)`.\n\nActually, looking at the overload:\n```cpp\ntemplate <class Shape, class Stride, class IntTuple>\nCUTE_HOST_DEVICE constexpr\nauto\ncoalesce_x(Layout<Shape,Stride> const& layout, IntTuple const& trg_profile)\n{\n  if constexpr (is_tuple<IntTuple>::value) {\n    ...\n    return transform_layout(layout, trg_profile, ...);\n  } else {\n    return coalesce_x(layout);\n  }\n}\n```\n\nSo if RHS is rank-1 (non-tuple), we just call `coalesce_x(layout)` without the profile.\n\nThe `coalesce_x` function:\n```cpp\ntemplate <class Shape, class Stride>\nCUTE_HOST_DEVICE constexpr\nauto\ncoalesce_x(Layout<Shape,Stride> const& layout)\n{\n  auto flat_shape  = flatten(layout.shape());\n  auto flat_stride = flatten(layout.stride());\n\n  constexpr int R = decltype(rank(flat_shape))::value;\n  if constexpr (is_constant<1, decltype(get<R-1>(flat_shape))>::value) {\n    return detail::bw_coalesce<R-2>(flat_shape, flat_stride, Int<2>{}, get<R-1>(flat_stride));\n  } else {\n    return detail::bw_coalesce<R-2>(flat_shape, flat_stride, get<R-1>(flat_shape), get<R-1>(flat_stride));\n  }\n}\n```\n\nWait, `coalesce_x` uses `Int<2>{}` for the base case when the last shape is 1? That seems weird. Let me look at `bw_coalesce`:\n\n```cpp\ntemplate <int I, class OldShape, class OldStride, class NewShape, class NewStride>\nCUTE_HOST_DEVICE constexpr\nauto\nbw_coalesce(OldShape const& old_shape, OldStride const& old_stride,\n            NewShape const& new_shape, NewStride const& new_stride)\n{\n  if constexpr (I == -1) {\n    if constexpr (is_constant<1, NewShape>::value) {\n      return Layout<_1,_0>{};\n    } else {\n      return Layout<NewShape,NewStride>{new_shape,new_stride};\n    }\n  } else if constexpr (is_constant<1, decltype(get<I>(old_shape))>::value) {\n    return bw_coalesce<I-1>(old_shape, old_stride, new_shape, new_stride);\n  } else if constexpr (is_constant<1, NewShape>::value) {\n    return bw_coalesce<I-1>(old_shape, old_stride, get<I>(old_shape), get<I>(old_stride));\n  } else if constexpr (...merge condition...) {\n    return bw_coalesce<I-1>(old_shape, old_stride,\n                            replace_front(new_shape, get<I>(old_shape) * get<0>(new_shape)),\n                            replace_front(new_stride, get<I>(old_stride)));\n  } else {\n    // Can't replace or merge, so prepend a new mode\n    return bw_coalesce<I-1>(old_shape, old_stride,\n                            prepend(new_shape, get<I>(old_shape)),\n                            prepend(new_stride, get<I>(old_stride)));\n  }\n}\n```\n\nOK, now I understand `bw_coalesce` - it's a backward coalescing pass. It starts from the end of the layout and works forward. The merge condition checks if `old_shape[i] * old_stride[i] == new_stride[0]`. If so, they can be merged into one mode.\n\nNow, the critical `composition_impl` function for the case where LHS has a tuple shape and RHS has an integral shape (the \"general case\"):\n\nThe fold iterates over modes of LHS (0 to R-2), and for each mode:\n1. Compute `next_shape = ceil(curr_shape / abs(rest_stride))`\n2. Compute `next_stride = ceil(abs(rest_stride) / curr_shape) * signum(rest_stride)`\n3. If `next_shape == 1` or `rest_shape == 1`, skip (don't add a mode to result)\n4. Otherwise, `new_shape = min(next_shape, rest_shape)`, add mode with shape `new_shape` and stride `rest_stride * curr_stride`\n5. Update `rest_shape = rest_shape / new_shape` and `rest_stride = next_stride`\n\nAfter the fold:\n- If result has no modes: return Layout(rest_shape, rest_stride * lhs_stride[R-1])\n- If rest_shape == 1: return Layout(result_shape, result_stride)\n- Otherwise: append rest_shape and rest_stride * lhs_stride[R-1]\n\nLet me trace this through the example:\nA = Layout((4, 3), (2, 8)), B = Layout(3, 2)\n\nAfter coalescing A: 12:2 (rank-1)\n\nNow composition_impl(lhs_shape=12, lhs_stride=2, rhs_shape=3, rhs_stride=2):\n\nLHS shape is integral (12), so: Layout(3, 2*2) = Layout(3, 4) = 3:4 â\n\nLet me try another example. A = Layout((4, 3), (2, 8)), B = Layout(6, 1):\n\ncoalesce(A) = 12:2\ncomposition_impl(12, 2, 6, 1):\nLHS shape is integral: Layout(6, 1*2) = 6:2\n\nCheck: R(k) = A(k) for k in [0,5]: 0, 2, 4, 6, 8, 10 â\n\nNow let me try A = Layout((4, 3), (1, 8)), B = Layout(6, 1):\n\ncoalesce(A) = can't coalesce â (4,3):(1,8)\n\nAfter coalesce_x: since R=2, and the last shape (3) is not 1, so result = bw_coalesce<0>(flat_shape, flat_stride, 3, 8)\n\nI=0: get<0>(old_shape) = 4, which is not 1.\nNewShape = 3, which is not 1.\nCheck merge: old_shape[0] * old_stride[0] = 4 * 1 = 4, new_stride[0] = 8. 4 != 8, can't merge.\nSo prepend: bw_coalesce<-1>(..., (4, 3), (1, 8))\n\nI == -1: not constant 1. Return Layout((4,3), (1,8)).\n\nSo A stays (4,3):(1,8) after coalesce.\n\nNow composition_impl with lhs_shape=(4,3), lhs_stride=(1,8), rhs_shape=6, rhs_stride=1:\n\nLHS shape is tuple, so we use the general case. R=2.\n\nfold over [0]:\n\ninit = ((), (), 6, 1)\n\ni=0:\n- curr_shape = 4, curr_stride = 1\n- rest_shape = 6, rest_stride = 1\n- next_shape = ceil(4 / |1|) = 4\n- next_stride = ceil(|1| / 4) * 1 = 1\n- next_shape = 4, rest_shape = 6 â neither is 1\n- new_shape = min(4, 6) = 4\n- result_shape = (4,), result_stride = (1*1,) = (1,)\n- rest_shape = 6 / 4 = 1.5 â hmm\n\nWait, that's not an integer! This means the composition is not valid or the LHS doesn't divide B properly.\n\nActually, let me re-examine. cecka says the divisibility conditions are checked (weakly or strongly).\n\nIn this example, B = Layout(6, 1) means B(0)=0, B(1)=1, B(2)=2, B(3)=3, B(4)=4, B(5)=5.\nA = (4,3):(1,8) means A(0)=0, A(1)=1, A(2)=2, A(3)=3, A(4)=8, A(5)=9, A(6)=10, A(7)=11, A(8)=16, A(9)=17, A(10)=18, A(11)=19.\n\nR(k) = A(B(k)):\nR(0)=0, R(1)=1, R(2)=2, R(3)=3, R(4)=8, R(5)=9.\n\nThis is not a simple rank-1 layout. It should be something like (6):(1) with some breaks. But actually, 0,1,2,3,8,9 doesn't fit any regular layout.\n\nR is: 0,1,2,3,8,9. The strides between consecutive elements are: 1,1,1,5,1. This isn't a regular layout!\n\nSo this example is actually not a valid composition input (the \"divisibility condition\" fails). In CUTLASS, this would be a compile-time assertion failure or a runtime assertion.\n\nOK, so the key insight is: the composition algorithm assumes certain divisibility conditions hold, and if they do, the result is a valid layout.\n\nLet me trace through a more complex but valid example.\n\nA = Layout((4, 3), (2, 8)), B = Layout(6, 1):\ncoalesce(A) = 12:2 (since 4*2=8 == stride 8, can merge)\ncomposition_impl(12, 2, 6, 1): integral LHS â Layout(6, 2)\n\nA = Layout((2, 3), (3, 8)), B = Layout(6, 1):\ncoalesce(A): 2*3=6 != 8, can't merge â (2,3):(3,8)\n\nWait, but B(5)=5, A(5):\ncrd2idx(5, (2,3), (3,8)) = 5%2=1, 5//2=2 â 1*3 + 2*8 = 19\n\nR(k) = A(k):\n0â0, 1â3, 2â6, 3â9, 4â8, 5â11\n\nStrides: 3, 3, 3, -1, 3 â not regular.\n\nHmm, so this is also not a valid input. Let me find a valid one...\n\nActually, let's try: A = Layout((4, 3), (3, 16)), B = Layout(6, 1):\n\ncoalesce(A): 4*3=12 != 16, can't merge â (4,3):(3,16)\n\nA(0)=0, A(1)=3, A(2)=6, A(3)=9, A(4)=16, A(5)=19...\n\nR(k) = A(k) for k=0..5: 0, 3, 6, 9, 16, 19\nStrides: 3, 3, 3, 7, 3 â not regular.\n\nOK, what about: A = Layout((4, 6), (1, 8)), B = Layout(6, 2):\n\ncoalesce(A): 4*1=4 != 8, can't merge â (4,6):(1,8)\n\nB(k) = 2k for k=0..5: 0, 2, 4, 6, 8, 10\n\nA(0)=0, A(2)=2, A(4)=4, A(6)=16, A(8)=8, A(10)=10\n\nA(6) = crd2idx(6, (4,6), (1,8)) = 6%4=2, 6//4=1 â 2*1 + 1*8 = 10. Can this be a layout?\n\n0,2 â stride 2\n8-2=6 â different stride\n10-8=2 â stride 2\n16-10=6 â different\n18-16=2 â stride 2\n\nNot rank-1. What about rank-2?\n\nIf R = (a, b):(d0, d1) with 6 = a*b:\n- 0, 2, 8, 10, 16, 18\n\nFor a=2: \n- j=0: 0, 2 â d0=2\n- j=1: 8, 10 â 8-0=8=d1? d0*(a-1)+d1 = 2+d1=? and second row starts at 8. d1=8.\n- j=2: 16, 18 â d1*2=16, and 18-16=2=d0 â\n\nSo R = (2, 3):(2, 8).\n\nLet's verify with the algorithm:\nlhs_shape = (4, 6), lhs_stride = (1, 8), rhs_shape = 6, rhs_stride = 2\n\nR = 2, fold over [0]:\n\ninit = ((), (), 6, 2)\n\ni=0:\n- curr_shape = 4, curr_stride = 1\n- rest_shape = 6, rest_stride = 2\n- next_shape = ceil(4 / |2|) = ceil(4/2) = 2\n- next_stride = ceil(|2| / 4) * signum(2) = 1 * 1 = 1\n- next_shape=2, rest_shape=6 â neither is 1\n- new_shape = min(2, 6) = 2\n- result_shape = (2,), result_stride = (2*1,) = (2,)\n- rest_shape = 6 / 2 = 3\n- rest_stride = 1\n\nAfter fold:\n- result_shape = (2,), result_stride = (2,)\n- rest_shape = 3, rest_stride = 1\n- tuple_size > 0 and rest_shape != 1\n- Output: Layout((2, 3), (2, 1*8)) = Layout((2, 3), (2, 8)) â\n\nNow let me implement this in Python.\n\nThe key cases in the C++ code:\n\n1. RHS shape is tuple â right-distributivity: compose each mode of RHS with the LHS (this is the \"B.shape is hierarchical\" case)\n\n2. RHS stride is 0 â return Layout(rhs_shape, 0)\n\n3. LHS shape is integral (rank-1 after coalescing) â return Layout(rhs_shape, rhs_stride * lhs_stride)\n\n4. General case (LHS is tuple, RHS is integral) â the fold algorithm\n\nNow, the top-level `composition` function:\n```cpp\ncomposition(lhs, rhs):\n  flat_lhs = coalesce_x(lhs, coprofile(rhs))\n  return composition_impl(flat_lhs.shape, flat_lhs.stride, rhs.shape, rhs.stride)\n```\n\nWhen rhs is a Layout (rank-1), `coprofile(rhs)` returns something with the structure of rhs's stride (which is just an integer for rank-1).\n\nWait, looking more carefully at `coalesce_x`:\n```cpp\ntemplate <class Shape, class Stride, class IntTuple>\nCUTE_HOST_DEVICE constexpr\nauto\ncoalesce_x(Layout<Shape,Stride> const& layout, IntTuple const& trg_profile)\n{\n  if constexpr (is_tuple<IntTuple>::value) {\n    static_assert(tuple_size<IntTuple>::value <= Layout<Shape,Stride>::rank);\n    return transform_layout(layout, trg_profile, ...);\n  } else {\n    return coalesce_x(layout);\n  }\n}\n```\n\nSo when `trg_profile` (coprofile of RHS) is not a tuple (i.e., RHS is rank-1), we just call `coalesce_x(layout)`, which flattens and coalesces.\n\nFor the other overload of `composition` that takes a Tiler (non-Layout):\n```cpp\ntemplate <class LShape, class LStride, class Tiler>\nCUTE_HOST_DEVICE constexpr\nauto\ncomposition(Layout<LShape,LStride> const& lhs, Tiler const& rhs)\n{\n  if constexpr (is_tuple<Tiler>::value) {\n    // Apply composition element-wise\n    return detail::transform_layout(lhs, rhs, ...);\n  } else if constexpr (is_underscore<Tiler>::value) {\n    return lhs;\n  } else if constexpr (is_integral<Tiler>::value) {\n    auto flat_lhs = detail::coalesce_x(lhs);\n    return detail::composition_impl(flat_lhs.shape(), flat_lhs.stride(), rhs, Int<1>{});\n  }\n}\n```\n\nWhen RHS is an integer: coalesce_x(lhs), then composition_impl with rhs_shape=rhs, rhs_stride=1.\n\nOK, now I need to implement this in Python. Let me map the C++ algorithm to the Python API.\n\nThe task says:\n1. `layoutB is None`: return layoutA unchanged\n2. `layoutB` is an integer: treat as Layout(layoutB)\n3. `layoutB` is a tuple: compose each mode of layoutA with matching entry\n4. `layoutB.shape` is hierarchical: compose layoutA with each mode of layoutB\n5. stride-zero layoutB: return stride-zero with layoutB.shape\n6. general rank-1 layoutB: use coalesced modes of layoutA\n\nLet me implement each case:\n\nCase 1: return layoutA\nCase 2: B = Layout(layoutB), then fall through to case 6 with B.stride = 1 (since Layout(N) = Layout(N, prefix_product(N)) = Layout(N, N)... wait, for Layout(N), stride = prefix_product(N) = N if N is a scalar. Hmm, but Layout(N) for an integer N creates N:N (shape N, stride N).\n\nWait, actually: Layout(N) with just shape N:\n```python\ndef __init__(self, _shape, _stride=None):\n    self.shape = _shape\n    if _stride is None:\n        self.stride = prefix_product(self.shape)\n    else:\n        self.stride = _stride\n```\n\nFor Layout(N) where N is int, prefix_product(N) = N. So Layout(N) = Layout(N, N).\n\nBut in the CUTLASS code, composition with an integer RHS uses `rhs, Int<1>{}` (stride=1). This is a \"subsetting\" of A.\n\nThese are very different! Which one does the task want?\n\nThe task says \"layoutB is an integer: treat as Layout(layoutB)\". So Layout(layoutB) = Layout(N, N). Then this falls through to case 6 (general rank-1 B with stride 1).\n\nOK, good. Let me now implement the composition function.\n\nNow, let me also understand the case where B is a tuple. From the CUTLASS code:\n\n```cpp\ntemplate <class LShape, class LStride, class Tiler>\nauto composition(Layout<LShape,LStride> const& lhs, Tiler const& rhs)\n{\n  if constexpr (is_tuple<Tiler>::value) {\n    return detail::transform_layout(lhs, rhs, [](auto const& l, auto const& r) { return composition(l,r); }, \n                                     make_seq<tuple_size<Tiler>::value>{}, seq<>{}, seq<>{});\n  }\n  ...\n}\n```\n\nThis composes each mode of lhs with the matching entry of rhs. The transform_layout function takes elements from both lhs and rhs, and applies composition(l, r) element-wise. For excess elements in lhs (beyond rhs's length), they're kept unchanged.\n\nIn the Python code, this corresponds to: for each mode i, if B[i] is None, keep A[i]; otherwise compose A[i] with B[i].\n\nNow for the case where B.shape is a tuple (hierarchical):\n\n```cpp\nif constexpr (is_tuple<RShape>::value) {\n    return transform_layout(rhs_shape, rhs_stride, [&](auto const& s, auto const& d) {\n      return composition_impl(lhs_shape, lhs_stride, s, d);\n    });\n}\n```\n\nThis decomposes B into its modes and composes the entire LHS with each mode.\n\nWait, but `composition_impl` is called here, not `composition`. None entries are no-ops for that mode.\"\n\nThis aligns with the CUTLASS overload that takes a Tiler (tuple). But in the CUTLASS code, this first coalesces A... actually, no. The Tiler overload doesn't coalesce first. Let me re-read:\n\n```cpp\ntemplate <class LShape, class LStride, class Tiler>\nauto composition(Layout<LShape,LStride> const& lhs, Tiler const& rhs)\n{\n  if constexpr (is_tuple<Tiler>::value) {\n    static_assert(tuple_size<Tiler>::value <= Layout<LShape,LStride>::rank);\n    return detail::transform_layout(lhs, rhs, [](auto const& l, auto const& r) { return composition(l,r); }, \n                                     make_seq<tuple_size<Tiler>::value>{}, seq<>{}, seq<>{});\n  }\n```\n\nSo when rhs is a tuple of layouts, it applies composition(l, r) element-wise to the modes of lhs. Let me look at the Python make_layout:\n\n```python\ndef make_layout(*layouts):\n    if len(layouts) == 1 and not is_layout(layouts[0]):\n        layouts = layouts[0]\n\n    shape, stride = zip(*((a.shape, a.stride) for a in layouts))\n    return Layout(shape, stride)\n```\n\nSo make_layout takes multiple Layouts and creates a hierarchical layout with tuple shape and stride.\n\nOK, for the case where B.shape is a tuple:\n\nLooking at the CUTLASS composition_impl, when RHS shape is tuple:\n```cpp\nif constexpr (is_tuple<RShape>::value) {\n    return transform_layout(rhs_shape, rhs_stride, [&](auto const& s, auto const& d) {\n      return composition_impl(lhs_shape, lhs_stride, s, d);\n    });\n}\n```\n\n`transform_layout` here applies composition_impl to each (s, d) pair from rhs_shape and rhs_stride, and the result is a tuple of layouts.\n\nBut wait, `rhs` here is already a Layout with tuple shape.
